root.App.Cache.genUrl = function (routeName, context) {
        var route = routeMap[routeName],
            path, keys, i, len, key, param, regex;

        if (!route) { return ''; }

        path = route.path;
        keys = route.keys;

        if (context &amp;&amp; (len = keys.length)) {
            for (i = 0; i &lt; len; i += 1) {
                key   = keys[i];
                param = key.name || key;
                regex = new RegExp('[:*]' + param + '\\b');
                path  = path.replace(regex, context[param]);
            }
        }

        // Replace missing params with empty strings.
        return path.replace(/([:*])([\w\-]+)?/g, '');
    };

the Costly Reality of Run-Flat Tires","summary":"Ready to tackle this misfortune, he looked for a spare tire in the trunk, but there was none to be found.  Without the option to solve the dilemma on his own, he called BMW roadside assistance, only to be told there was no spare tire since the car comes with run-flats.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w900\u002F1a7c120c1180539356f36886dd992bc0a13bb240.jpg\" alt=\"Deflating the Costly Reality of Run-Flat Tires\" width=\"900\" height=\"647\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ERun-flat tires promise to remove a key travel worry&#x2014;being stranded roadside. However, the ownership experience can be both expensive and frustrating, as we have heard from owners.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EA reader recently recounted a nightmarish run-flat tire tale that captures the potential downsides to this technology and mirrors other feedback we have received. (Even our staff has had their own run-flat adventures.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThis consumer wrote us about driving his dream car, a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fbmw\u002F5-series\u002F2016\u002F4dr-sdn-550i-rwd\"\u003E2012 BMW 550i\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, on a long trip. When a tire-pressure warning light illuminated, he pulled off the highway, stopped, and discovered a flat tire. Ready to tackle this misfortune, he looked for a spare tire in the trunk, but there was none to be found.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWithout the option to solve the dilemma on his own, he called \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fbmw\u002F\"\u003EBMW\u003C\u002Fa\u003E roadside assistance, only to be told there was no spare tire since the car comes with run-flats.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBecause the flat was caused by a sidewall failure, the owner was told not to drive on it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ELate on a Sunday night, far from home, the driver spent 2 &#xBD; hours waiting for a flat-bed tow to get the expensive car to safe ground, followed by an unexpected night in a hotel. &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe disappointed owner got his car back on the road the next day and was fairly satisfied knowing flats are a rare event. But he felt that he would have bought a different car with regular tires instead of the run-flats, had he known.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESince the initial troublesome experience, the owner was stranded four more times, accumulating a total of eight road-hazard flats in less than 30,000 miles. Adding insult to injury, in the best of times, the owner found the run-flats to be stiff riding and noisy. Plus, they cost a bundle to replace (claimed $500 apiece) and even at that, replacements are hard to find.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"700\" height=\"374\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w700\u002F37b3c783643327ce7f252c550d7f3155b2f00501.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003Ci\u003ERun-flat tires are standard with many luxury vehicles like the BMW 5 Series, pictured here.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAlthough eight failures is extreme for any car, the issues related to comfort and replacement are not unique to this individual. We&#x2019;ve heard them similar complaints from many others. In this case, a BMW dealer suggested he buy tire insurance for a mere $2,500&#x2014;an astronomical sum that sounded ridiculous at the time. To be fair, the owner confided a BMW dealer did make some concessions on the cost of some of the replacement tires, but he no longer has confidence in his beloved car.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe owner suggests that anyone buying a car with run-flats inquire about tire insurance and negotiate the price down to make the car deal happen. We estimate that about 15 percent of the cars sold last year came with run-flats, so be sure to ask the dealer what kind of tires are on the car before you buy it. Many cars today come with just a tire repair kit, rather than a spare tire. Be sure you are getting what you expect when you buy a car, and if it doesn&#x2019;t include a spare, ask if one is available.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHave you experienced the benefits, or frustrations, with run-flat tires? Share your insights in the comments below.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x2014;\u003Cem\u003EGene Petersen\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EMore from Consumer Reports:\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.consumerreports.org\u002Fcro\u002Fnews\u002F2015\u002F03\u002Ften-for-the-long-haul\u002Findex.htm?EXTKEY=AYAHFP03\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003EBest cars for making it to 200,000 miles\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.consumerreports.org\u002Fcro\u002Fmagazine\u002F2015\u002F06\u002F10-great-used-cars-under-10000-dollars\u002Findex.htm?EXTKEY=AYAHFP04\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003E10 great used cars for under $10,00 for teens\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.consumerreports.org\u002Fcro\u002Fnews\u002F2014\u002F06\u002F10-midlife-crisis-cars-for-father-s-day\u002Findex.htm?EXTKEY=AYAHFP05\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003E10 midlife crisis cars\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EConsumer Reports has no relationship with any advertisers on this website. Those 5-Star Ratings--Why Bigger is Safer","summary":"GM, Ford, FCA Kick Off Negotiations with UAW IIHS offset crash test of the Toyota Camry and Toyota Corolla By Paul A. Eisenstein While conventional wisdom has a way of being wrong, a new study by the University of Buffalo suggests that, when it comes to cars, one traditional belief is correct: bigger cars tend to be safer cars.  The bottom line, according to a study presented during the annual meeting of the Society for Academic Emergency Medicine, is that bigger, more expensive vehicles tend to be the safest.  The most important point of our study is that vehicle weight and price have a positive relationship with vehicle safety, said Dr. Dietrich Jehle, a professor of emergency medicine at University of Buffalo School of Medicine and Biomedical Sciences, who presented the research.  Researchers say that no matter how good the crash rating is on a car like the Honda Civic, its not as safe as a bigger vehicle, such as an F-150.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.thedetroitbureau.com\u002F2015\u002F07\u002Fgm-ford-fca-kick-off-negotiations-with-uaw\u002F\" title=\"Permanent Link to GM, Ford, FCA Kick Off Negotiations with UAW\"\u003EGM, Ford, FCA Kick Off Negotiations with UAW\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F0a207e7a77e1bea0630729addad52c2bad6a81fc.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"361\" alt=\"Forget Those 5-Star Ratings--Why Bigger is Safer\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EIIHS offset crash test of the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Ftoyota\u002Fcamry\u002F\"\u003EToyota Camry\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Ftoyota\u002Fcorolla\"\u003EToyota Corolla\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBy Paul A. Eisenstein\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhile conventional wisdom has a way of being wrong, a new study by the University of Buffalo suggests that, when it comes to cars, one traditional belief is correct: bigger cars tend to be safer cars.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhile even some of the smallest cars on the market today earn five-star crash ratings, it doesn&#x2019;t necessarily reflect what happens in the real world &#x2013; especially when that little car smashes into a big one or, worse, an 18-wheeler. The bottom line, according to a study presented during the annual meeting of the Society for Academic Emergency Medicine, is that bigger, more expensive vehicles tend to be the safest.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;The most important point of our study is that vehicle weight and price have a positive relationship with vehicle safety,&#x201D; said Dr. Dietrich Jehle, a professor of emergency medicine at University of Buffalo School of Medicine and Biomedical Sciences, who presented the research.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"337\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F450b4f25b7fc02b1119c865eb4e12ff59eb436a0.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EResearchers say that no matter how good the crash rating is on a car like the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fhonda\u002Fcivic-sedan\u002F\"\u003EHonda Civic\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, it&#x2019;s not as safe as a bigger vehicle, such as an \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fford\u002Ff-150\u002F\"\u003EF-150\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe study upends conventional industry data. Using their own methodology, U-B researchers place such popular vehicles as the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fhonda\u002Faccord-sedan\u002F\"\u003EHonda Accord\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and Civic, as well as the Toyota Corolla, in their &#x201C;least safe&#x201D; category. They had 40% more injuries than the industry average, according to the study.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAt the other extreme are such large vehicles as the Ford F-150, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fland-rover\u002Frange-rover\u002F\"\u003ERange Rover\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fchevrolet\u002Fsilverado-1500\u002F\"\u003EChevrolet Silverado\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fcadillac\u002Fescalade\"\u003ECadillac Escalade\u003C\u002Fa\u003E ESV. One notable exception to the bigger-is-better rule: the &#x201C;safest&#x201D; list includes the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fmini\u002Fcooper-countryman\u002F\"\u003EMini Cooper Countryman\u003C\u002Fa\u003E &#x2013; which is, nonetheless, the British maker&#x2019;s biggest product line.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe study found that the safety of the average vehicle increased by 19% for every 1,000 pounds of additional weight, while there was a 12% improvement for every additional $10,000 in a vehicle&#x2019;s price tag.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;One of my pet peeves is that I don&#x2019;t think consumers have very good information about vehicle safety,&#x201D; Jehle said. &#x201C;Neither media advertising nor the five-star safety ratings accurately reflect the level of danger or lack of danger in vehicles.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F25126df0a42de3d5335ecda4234329f2034702a5.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe Buffalo study was based on a retrospective study of 360 different vehicle models from 2010 to 2012 and used Highway Loss Data Institute, or HLDI, data to calculate real world injuries. The new study tried to accommodate the fact that some vehicles are driven significantly more than others and, among other things, excluded sports cars because they typically clock relatively few miles.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBy comparison, the National Highway Traffic Safety Administration and the Insurance Institute for Highway Safety, base their ratings on crash tests in which vehicles are normally run into fixed barriers. But that may not be a particularly accurate reflection of what happens in the real world, especially when a small car and a big pickup lock horns, the study warns.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;When smaller cars hit a larger, moving vehicle, that change in velocity can force the smaller car to go into reverse, resulting in far more serious injuries to driver and passenger,&#x201D; said Jehle.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe study cautions that cost and weight don&#x2019;t always seem to be the final determinant of crash safety. The Mini Countryman and Jeep Wrangler both had an average 40% fewer personal injury claims. The \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fvolkswagen\u002Fgolf\"\u003EVolkswagen Golf\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and the Subaru Outback scored more than 25% better than average. But, on the whole, big pickups and large SUVs tended to top the chart, while small vehicles such as the Honda Civic, Ford Fiesta and Kia Forte had much higher-than-average injury claims.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe study raises some potentially troubling issues for the auto industry at a time when manufacturers are putting heavy emphasis, as it were, on lightweighting. The newest, &#x201C;aluminum-intensive&#x201D; version of the Ford F-150 is, for example, about 700 pounds lighter than the steel-bodied version included in the U-B study. And most products are expected to continue getting lighter in the push for better fuel economy.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore at The Detroit Bureau\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.thedetroitbureau.com\u002F2015\u002F07\u002Fgm-ford-fca-kick-off-negotiations-with-uaw\u002F\" title=\"Permanent Link to GM, Ford, FCA Kick Off Negotiations with UAW\"\u003EGM, Ford, FCA Kick Off Negotiations with UAW\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ca &#x201C;More Muscular&#x201D; Auto Safety Oversight &#x2013; and Congress Ready to Help\"\u003EFeds Aim for &#x201C;More Muscular&#x201D; Auto Safety Oversight &#x2013; and Congress Ready to TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fd1f2d4d70c1d761641f79d4effeea138b0d4b0f8.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":540,"height":304,"size_type":"original","formats":{}}],"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002Foriginal\u002FsApsuP1pFGKGDGg2pMHIldO9_NU","source_url":"http:\u002F\u002F40.media.tumblr.com\u002F59a194841052515ffc3353ea565c59da\u002Ftumblr_inline_nrfyhacVIn1rmmdbb_540.jpg"}],"highlight_color":"#000000","data_version":"1","title":"Teen Truckers? Congress Considers Letting Them Drive Big Rigs","summary":"Parents may hesitate to hand teens the keys to the family car, but Congress is proposing to allow drivers as young as 18 to get behind the wheel of 18-wheelers.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fd1f2d4d70c1d761641f79d4effeea138b0d4b0f8.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"304\" alt=\"Teen Truckers? Congress Considers Letting Them Drive Big Rigs\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EParents may hesitate to hand teens the keys to the family car, but Congress is proposing to allow drivers as young as 18 to get behind the wheel of big rigs on the nation&#x2019;s interstates &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFederal regulations currently require drivers be at least 21 before they can drive commercial trucks across state lines, but a bill introduced this week by Republican senators would allow contiguous states that join together in &#x201C;compacts&#x201D; to drop the age threshold to 18 for interstate trips. There is no limit on the number of states that could join the compacts. &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAfter four years, the Transportation secretary is supposed to report to Congress on whether teens have &#x201C;an equivalent level of safety&#x201D; in comparison with older truckers. &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn 2013, all drivers ages 18-20 had a fatal crash involvement rate, per 100,000 licensed drivers, that was 66 percent higher than drivers who were age 21 years or older, according to the Transportation Department&#x2019;s Fatality Analysis Reporting System, although the total number of crash deaths among teens has been declining since 2002. &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe change was sought by the trucking industry to help address a shortage of truck drivers. The American Trucking Associations estimates that the current shortage of drivers is roughly 35,000 to 40,000, but because of retirements and individuals leaving the industry, trucking companies will need to recruit nearly 100,000 new drivers a year over the next decade to keep pace with the country&#x2019;s freight needs. &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut Jackie Gillan, president of Advocates for Highway and Auto Safety, said allowing teens to drive trucks weighing as much as 80,000 pounds and to work as many as 82 hours a week, as is permitted in the truck industry, is a &#x201C;catastrophe waiting to happen.&#x201D; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;The combination of inexperience, high-risk driving and large trucks can cause unbelievable devastation,&#x201D; she said. &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDave Osiecki, chief of advocacy for trucking associations, said states already allow teens to drive commercial trucks unlimited miles within their borders. For example, it makes no sense to allow a teen truck driver to drive hundreds of miles from one end to the other of a state like Virginia, but prohibit the same driver from crossing the Potomac River into Washington, he said. &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;We absolutely support&#x201D; lowering the age limit, he said. &#x201C;It would be good for our industry, it would be good for commerce, it would be good for the economy.&#x201D; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELegislation to allow states to lower the age for a commercial, interstate license to 18 was first introduced by Sen. Deb Fischer, R-Neb., and was incorporated into a larger transportation bill introduced this week by Senate Commerce Committee Chairman John Thune, R-S.D., Sen. Jerry Moran, R-Kan., and Fischer. &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe bill would restrict teen truckers from hauling hazardous materials or operating &#x201C;special configurations,&#x201D; which are generally defined as oversized or overweight loads. States and the U.S. Department of Transportation would also be allowed impose other restrictions if they wish. &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EStates wouldn&#x2019;t be obligated to join the compacts, but Gillan said she expects state officials would be under pressure from trucking industry to do so.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETo obtain an interstate commercial driver&#x2019;s license, drivers must pass a written knowledge test and a driving skills test administered by a state motor vehicles department. But there is no requirement that drivers first receive on the road training or attend a training school, Gillan said. &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0;&#xA0;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELabor unions have said the driver shortage could be eliminated by raising truckers&#x2019; wages and improving working conditions. &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EA decade ago the Bush administration looked at lowering the commercial truck driving age to 18, but ultimately decided against doing that because the public comments the government received were overwhelmingly against the idea. &#xA0; &#xA0; Scion iM: First Drive","summary":"Trying to recapture its hipness, Scion brings over the iM, a hatchback with a balance of features and performance that's a bargain in its class.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWhat is it?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E A five-door compact hatchback\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EPrice range:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E$18,460 (manual), $19,200 (automatic)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ECompetitors:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fhyundai\u002Felantra\u002F\"\u003EHyundai Elantra\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fmazda\u002Fmazda3\u002F\"\u003EMazda3\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fvolkswagen\u002Fgolf\"\u003EVolkswagen Golf\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EAlternatives:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fford\u002Ffocus\"\u003EFord Focus\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fsubaru\u002Fimpreza\u002F\"\u003ESubaru Impreza \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EPros:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E It&#x2019;s a great value, a somewhat sporty, handsome looking hatch, with a sophisticated cabin, plenty of cargo room and stellar handling for not a lot of money. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ECons:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E Lacks the get-up-and-go of its peers. And thus, was just not as fun to drive. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWould I buy it with my money?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E I&#x2019;m on the fence here. The iM is a solid value in the compact category, but I would prefer a zippier machine with more style.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F1807fa686c90b41bb8bf996cdef2ff90d2912189.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" alt=\"2016 Scion iM: First Drive\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EScion wants its mojo back. In 2003, Toyota&#x2019;s hip, trendy and youth-oriented marquee was the new kid on the block. Within three years, it was a legit player in the compact car arena, selling more than 173,000 units with only three models &#x2013; the xA, xB and tC &#x2013; in its stable. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EEver since that plateau, however, the wee brand has been on a steady decline, struggling to connect with buyers. Last year, for example, the brand sold only a smidge over 58,000 vehicles in the United States, and that&#x2019;s with a five-car lineup.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhat happened? Toyota allowed Scion&#x2019;s product to get stale and moldy. In so doing, it alienated demanding young buyers &#x2014; those who are typically unwilling to compromise on things like efficiency, looks, performance, and especially the latest technology &#x2014; that the company was conceived to attract in the first place.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ETo get its game back before turning into another Saturn, Scion is planning to put fresh metal in dealerships. On September 1, the four-door 2016 iA, Scion&#x2019;s first ever sedan, and the vehicle we are examining here, the 2016 Scion iM, will hit the streets all across the country.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut did automaker go far enough to recapture the hearts, minds and wallets of todays first-time car buyers?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F2bd26cbbce57dfb0779062348f9fc28a2d175746.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe iM began life as a Toyota Auris, a Corolla-based vehicle available in Europe and Japan. Scion gave it a more aggressive look, including an edgier front fascia with Piano Black accents and LED running lights. The car&#x2019;s sporting intent is further reinforced with a shapelier body kit. The differences between the Toyota and Scion are minimal; regardless, the vehicle remains a looker from any angle, just like the Auris. It just won&#x2019;t stand out from the crowd. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe interior is unmistakably Toyota. It looks great with plenty of soft-touch surfaces and superb fit and finish for this class. Standard fare is generous, as there are no factory options, at least not for the interior. Spacious is not an adjective that I&#x2019;d use to describe the iM&#x2019;s cabin, but it&#x2019;s not confining either. The seats are comfortable, and leg and head room is sufficient, even in the backseat.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EPowering the iM is a 1.8-liter four-cylinder DOHC 16-valve engine, the same found in the Corolla Eco model, featuring continuously variable valve timing and lift. More powerful than anything in the Auris line, it develops 137 hp and 126 pound-feet of torque, and comes mated to either a six-speed manual or a continuously variable automatic transmission that&#x2019;s equipped with a custom-tuned Sport mode that quickens throttle response and enhances the &#x201C;sporty nature of the electric power steering,&#x201D; whatever that means. The CVT also has a manual setting with seven imaginary gears.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"320\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F80248d0d3b6e4732ba53dbb3a4527870b476e18e.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOn the road, the iM doesn&#x2019;t present much of a threat to the perky Mazda 3 or fun-to-drive VW Golf in terms of overall performance. Feedback from the road is a bit lacking.&#xA0;However, it handles tight switchbacks and sweeping turns with equal aplomb.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe iM is quite miserly at the pumps, too. It&#x2019;s rated to deliver 27 mpg in the city and 36 on the highway for the manual model and 28 city\u002F37highway mpg for the CVT, two mpg better than the Corolla Eco. While these figures are good, they are not class leading. And given the power ratings of other hot hatches, such as the 155-hp Mazda 3, the 160-hp Ford Focus, and 170-hp VW Golf, the Scion should be better.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAs with all Scions, the 2016 iM will be offered in one trim. However, an array of dealer-installed options, such as a navigation upgrade for the infotainment system and an interior lighting kit, are available. A TRD package, complete with lowering springs, anti-roll bars, and an air filter, will also be offered by dealers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBottomline: The sporty five-door hatchback is an impressive machine considering its sub $20,000 price tag. It features some of the best balance between sport and comfort handling, and a relatively comprehensive feature set. Yes, it&#x2019;s comparative lack of power just doesn&#x2019;t blow our brains like some of the Euro-styled hatches on the market. But it does mark a step in the right direction for a company trying to get back on track. Of The Day: Who Pays if I Crash Into a Cow?","summary":"This is the first installation of a new Yahoo Autos feature, Question of the Day. Were scouring the Internet to uncover interesting questions and providing well-researched, professional advice.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fbc404384b9938ec03c0390d646e9bf6208e0a975.jpg\" alt=\"Question Of The Day: Who Pays if I Crash Into a Cow?\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPhoto credit: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.flickr.com\u002Fphotos\u002Fleszekleszczynski\u002F9325662885\u002Fin\u002Fphotolist-fd5sF8-7fpNh6-oe3j9Y-Kh5df-6eP3Lr-oxi45K-5uB9Yt-bWy1e3-cJYpef-6qNVZe-btS1N5-gqiPg8-t2a7o-nWHG2n-axrBrL-gWBGjC-nGNwBG-9NuLRm-9NuWMS-rHTECj-7UV5uo-ax27Sz-eUJbKs-udMcCr-fsh25x-oK8KUa-uT37zE-dMTsgn-2suKGh-ej1TZN-9VAJT5-cjdKwN-45gaGk-6k3mZP-bsQYbb-dwojvp-4ruELL-dzPQin-6qTbjN-6qT7HJ-8YsgDt-8Q6dVK-cYqVNb-am7YAf-appMYi-nBM8NA-5Y9xxE-o6RAt9-8obmSD-dLc1zq\"\u003ELeszek Leszczynski, Flickr\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThis is the first installation of a new Yahoo Autos feature, Question of the Day. We&#x2019;re scouring the Internet to uncover interesting questions that people have posted looking for advice from the unwashed masses. We will contact experts to give you well-researched, professional advice. You can also submit questions to autos_qotd@yahoo.com.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EToday&#x2019;s question comes from \u003Ci\u003EYahoo Answers\u003C\u002Fi\u003E:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fanswers.yahoo.com\u002Fquestion\u002Findex?qid=20150623203435AADB7Se&amp;soc_src=mail&amp;soc_trk=ma\"\u003E&#x201C;If I crash a car into a cow, will my insurance pay for crash or will the cow&#x2019;s owner pay for my dents?&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EAnswer:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E It may sound like a punch line, but there is nothing funny about hitting a cow with your car. Bad things happen when two tons of steel come into contact with 1,500 pounds of USDA prime. And the truth is, it happens more often than you might think.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EJust like crashes involving deer, livestock accidents can cause severe damage to your vehicle and serious injuries for the driver and passengers in the car. Unlike an incident with a deer, however, someone&#x2014;somewhere&#x2014;owns that cow. And Bessie? She&#x2019;s very valuable. So, are you on the hook for the loss of the cow? Is the cow&#x2019;s owner on the hook for the damage to your car? How much will your insurance cover?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe answers depend on several different factors, including the laws of the state where the accident occurred and the specifics of your auto insurance policy. For example, in Texas, a driver is not going to be liable for the value of the cow if the cow was running at large on a highway, but the rules are different for county or private roads. In other states, like Florida, there are specific fencing requirements that would make the owner of the cow liable for damages if the cow was on any public road. Even in that case though, it isn&#x2019;t all that simple for the driver because the driver would have to prove the cow&#x2019;s owner was \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.flsenate.gov\u002FLaws\u002FStatutes\u002F2012\u002F588.15\"\u003Enegligent\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOften, the issue of who owes what comes down to state and local laws about just these types of things: what type of road was it, was the cow&#x2019;s owner required to maintain secure fencing, was the fence properly maintained but somehow the cow got out, did the driver intentionally hit the cow? (Yes, there&#x2019;s an exception to the Texas law for drivers who show \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.statutes.legis.state.tx.us\u002Fdocs\u002FAG\u002Fhtm\u002FAG.143.htm\"\u003E&#x201C;wilful (sic) intent to strike, kill, injure, or damage the animal.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E Crazy, right?)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EEdward Smith, an attorney based in Sacramento, Calif., with over thirty years of experience handling livestock accidents whose firm maintains the website \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Flivestockaccident.com\u002F\"\u003Elivestockaccident.com\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, points to lack of awareness as a common mistake drivers make before even leaving the house. &#x201C;Many drivers from urban areas that travel for a day in the country do not realize that many counties in California and other states are &#x2018;open range.&#x2019;&#x201D; &#x2014; meaning either no or minimal duty to fence is required of cattle owners. Smith suggests that drivers in those areas need to exercise additional care, particularly when driving at night.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESo what should you do if you do careen into a cow on a lonesome highway? As with any accident, take care of the people and passengers first. Then call the police and report the accident. Take pictures of the scene. Smith points out that local law enforcement may not check on any fencing and ranchers can be quick to make repairs after an accident, so your pictures might be your best friend if you end up fighting over issues of liability.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EContact your insurance company as soon as practical. The pictures you took at the scene will help you out here, too. Accidents with animals fall under the comprehensive coverage portion of your policy. (This is optional coverage with a deductible so important to understand what type of insurance you have before you get into an accident. The Insurance Information Institute has a helpful \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.iii.org\u002Farticle\u002Finfographic-types-of-auto-coverage\"\u003Einfographic\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.) Ultimately, if you do end up needing a lawyer of your own, do some research and find someone who has experience handling livestock accidents.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E","content_status":"UNPUBLISHED","td_applet_infos":[],"canonical_urls":[],"uploaded_images":[],"type":"story","wiki_ids":[],"yct_categories":[],"privateTags":[],"leadImages":[{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w175\u002Fbc404384b9938ec03c0390d646e9bf6208e0a975.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":175,"height":117,"size_type":"175","formats":{},"types":{"image\u002Fjpeg":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w175\u002Fbc404384b9938ec03c0390d646e9bf6208e0a975.jpg"}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w200\u002Fbc404384b9938ec03c0390d646e9bf6208e0a975.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":200,"height":133,"size_type":"200","formats":{},"types":{"image\u002Fjpeg":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w200\u002Fbc404384b9938ec03c0390d646e9bf6208e0a975.jpg"}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w250\u002Fbc404384b9938ec03c0390d646e9bf6208e0a975.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":250,"height":167,"size_type":"250","formats":{},"types":{"image\u002Fjpeg":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w250\u002Fbc404384b9938ec03c0390d646e9bf6208e0a975.jpg"}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w300\u002Fbc404384b9938ec03c0390d646e9bf6208e0a975.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":300,"height":200,"size_type":"300","formats":{},"types":{"image\u002Fjpeg":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w300\u002Fbc404384b9938ec03c0390d646e9bf6208e0a975.jpg"}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w350\u002Fbc404384b9938ec03c0390d646e9bf6208e0a975.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":350,"height":233,"size_type":"350","formats":{},"types":{"image\u002Fjpeg":"https: Hottest Cars Among Collectors? Pickups","summary":"With prices for traditional classic cars soaring, would-be collectors have turned to the more affordable alternative  and sent sales skyward.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F51a564b9251a85dbe713d93771445c718c1ad58d.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"337\" alt=\"The Hottest Cars Among Collectors? Pickups\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E1949 Dodge B-Series\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAs the collector vehicle lifestyle continues to evolve, classic pickups have become the fastest growing segment among collectors. Analysis conducted by the Hagerty Valuation Team confirms the number of pickups purchased by collectors has grown more than any other collector vehicle segment. Pickups have seen a value growth of 56% over the past five years in correlation to other vehicle segments that show an average growth of 13%. Auction companies are supporting the trend as well; the number of classic pickups offered by the top 15 North American auction companies has doubled over the past three years.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"404\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F8a729b0129e50f3bed5dcc40df2b04cdc6fb5882.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E1950 Ford F-1\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;There was a time when trucks were only used by collectors to tow a car to the show, but now they are seriously collectible in their own right,&#x201D; says Hagerty CEO McKeel Hagerty. &#x201C;Classic pickups are also one of the easiest ways to enter the collector world. They are readily available, easy to work on and very affordable. I learned to drive on our 1933 Ford and have owned many collectible trucks since then.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to Hagerty&#x2019;s data, Ford and Chevrolet make up nearly 90% of all classic pickups currently on the road, and among the most popular are the 1960-72 Chevrolet C10s and 1961-72 Ford F-100s. Other makes are being noticed by collectors, as several generations of pickups are seeing significant value increases since 2010. Nissan Murano: Real World Review","summary":"How does the most stylish of crossovers perform in the dull reality of everyday driving?","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F7fa0e9e7f9d5938a200efabd81bd384af11fc7b7.jpg\" alt=\"2015 Nissan Murano: Real World Review\" width=\"540\" height=\"365\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWhat is it?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fnissan\u002Fmurano\u002F\"\u003E2015 Nissan Murano\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EPrice Range:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E $29,560 - $40,600\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ECompetitors:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fford\u002Fedge\u002F\"\u003EFord Edge\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fhonda\u002Fpilot\"\u003EHonda Pilot\u003C\u002Fa\u003E,&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fhyundai\u002Fsanta-fe\"\u003EHyundai Santa Fe\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fjeep\u002Fgrand-cherokee\u002F\"\u003EJeep Grand Cherokee\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EAlternatives:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Flexus\u002Frx-350\u002F\"\u003ELexus RX\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fhonda\u002Fpilot\"\u003EHonda Pilot\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Ftoyota\u002Fvenza\"\u003EToyota Venza\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EPros:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E Stand-out styling, technological bells and whistles.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ECons:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E Forgettable handling, middle-of-the-road performance.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWould I buy it with my own money?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E If I valued safety features and style over blander, more practical options, absolutely.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWalk outside to your nearest parking lot at work or school, and chances are you&#x2019;ll see a gathering as distinctive as a flock of sheep, stripped of character to maximize utility and homogenized to meet stringent standards. Nissan&#x2019;s 2015 Murano at first glance offers a reprieve from the mundane with what it calls the &#x201C;concept car for the street&#x201D;&#x2013;but alas, looks can be deceiving.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELike the boomerang headlights or not, the styling pops compared to all the sedate SUVs, especially in that iconic Pacific Sunset color. The curvaceous cockpit looks like it was designed by the Romulans, and the quartz trim offers a refreshing change from the simulated woods and metal touches typical for the segment. While Nissan tries to position the Murano as a quasi-luxury car, the materials inside are more like Honda than Volkswagen. Quality plastic is still plastic, but the futuristic cabin still has all the conventional knobs and dials you need, unlike Cadillac&#x2019;s CUE, or Ford&#x2019;s still-aggravating Sync.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Ff9f2399a18595870f8fb80879b1a0b325397621b.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhile the styling looks fitting for Tomorrowland, the driving experience is decidedly stuck in the present. Not as smooth as a Pathfinder or nimble as a Mazda CX-5, the handling strikes a lukewarm middle ground that&#x2019;s as memorable as picking up the keys to a midsize-something from Avis. It&#x2019;s not bad, mind you&#x2014;traction gives way to inevitable understeer, with mild body roll and adequate steering feedback. Sure, I have more fun flogging my dad&#x2019;s 2008 Honda Odyssey, but it&#x2019;s a compliant cruiser, thanks to the comfy &#x201C;Zero Gravity seats.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPower comes a-plenty from the 3.5-liter V6 making 260 horsepower, which won&#x2019;t send your heart racing as you effortlessly overtake slower traffic on mountain passes. (Unlike most gearless transmissions, the Nissan CVT unit doesn&#x2019;t force the engine into a constant motorboat sound). Its 21 city \u002F 28 highway mpg is in the same ballpark as other midsize SUVs, but even in all highway driving the most I could wring out was 26 mpg, and I averaged 25 mpg overall logging nearly 900 miles.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s more of an urban cruiser than ever, too, either. With the car-like ground clearance that has you scraping on steep driveways, and an AWD system that lacks torque vectoring, the Murano&#x2019;s idea of adventuring is picking up mulch from the local hardware store.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut there&#x2019;s more space for all your suburban hauling, with cargo volume growing to 39.6 cubic feet, which puts it between the Jeep Grand Cherokee&#x2019;s 36.3 and the Honda Pilot&#x2019;s 46.8. At this size you&#x2019;d start expecting a third row of seats though, since the Hyundai Santa Fe has them with a similar cargo volume of 40.9 cubic feet.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"354\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F1abfb875563d2792653f8c3bbebd70e9ecae4c5c.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhat does feel cutting edge is the safety tech. On the SL trim and up you get the Around View Monitor pulled from the Infiniti, giving a 360-degree view when pulling in and out of spots, making it the best parking assist available. The overzealously beeping Blind Spot Warning compensates for the sizable blockage created by the &#x201C;floating roof&#x201D; design treatment of the rear pillar, but it sets off even when there&#x2019;s plenty of room to make a lane change. On the flip side, the collision detection piece of the $2,260 technology package works perfect &#x2014; it&#x2019;s almost telepathic in knowing when you&#x2019;re distracted, and it doesn&#x2019;t set off prematurely like in a Subaru. In most cars I eventually get annoyed and shut it off, but actually appreciated the peace of mind in knowing it&#x2019;d intervene. These safety features make the Murano a compelling choice, especially since the SUV is a Top Safety Pick+ winner from the Insurance Institute of Highway Safety (IIHS).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHence it&#x2019;s still the function, not form, that&#x2019;s made the five-seat car-SUV combo the most popular type of new car. The aesthetically conscious crowd might go for a smaller&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Flexus\u002Fnx-200t\u002F\"\u003ELexus NX\u003C\u002Fa\u003E instead, and even if you&#x2019;re a fan of the Gundam styling, the top-level Platinum trim creeps into luxury-car prices at $39,885, placing it in the sights of the bigger competition like the Pilot or Jeep Grand Cherokee. No one said style was going to come for Reasons Youre Paying Hidden Dealer Fees","summary":"Car dealers have a well-deserved reputation for charging extra fees over the price you see on the sticker. Here's why people still pay them, and why you shouldn't.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fffbf3ec4c26da13232301300cb011242fb54417a.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"304\" alt=\"Three Reasons You&#x2019;re Paying Hidden Dealer Fees\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDoc fees. Processing fees. Finance fees. Even fees with weird initials instead of names that may or may not be named after the dealer&#x2019;s dog.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ECar dealers have a well-deserved reputation for charging extra fees over the price you see on the sticker. These add-ons can add $1,000 or more to the price of the car, and dealers have only grown more aggressive about them as profit margins on the metal itself have fallen. (Full disclosure: I&#x2019;ve owned my car dealership for well over 12 years now &#x2014; but my prices are all inclusive. I don&#x2019;t charge fees, and I tell folks not to pay them.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThose fees come in a variety of flavors &#x2014; delivery, document prep, VIN etching, even advertising fees and &#x201C;protection&#x201D; for things that are fairly well protected from the factory, like the underbody and seat fabrics.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut this rising tide of fees hasn&#x2019;t stopped car sales from surging to levels not seen in several years. And that&#x2019;s because of three things about our carbuying culture that work against the thrifty consumer:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EAmericans tend to focus only on the big numbers. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI&#x2019;m sure many of you have negotiated a deal for a rental property. They ask $1,200 for an apartment or a house, you may counter with $1,000.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut let me ask you. Did you also negotiate the amount of your deposit? &#xA0;Or the application fee? Chances are if you can easily afford these smaller costs, you probably did not. The same is true for re-financing on your home. Most folks will receive an estimate on the closing costs. But if the amounts in the final paperwork come out $500 to $700 ahead of those costs, they still sign on the dotted line. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPeople say they will always stick with a specific number no matter what. But if the smaller numbers in particular seem reasonable, they won&#x2019;t negotiate them so long as the deal seems reasonable. The American culture is unfortunately used to a degree of fudging and guess-timation, especially when the payments are spread over 72 months rather than all at once.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EEvery state has varying laws on what fees car dealers can and can&#x2019;t charge, and how they have to disclose it; many states have no limits, while in California dealers can only charge $80 max for shuffling paper. Generally speaking, you should eyeball every add-on, and question how they affect your rock-solid total, especially if they&#x2019;re not disclosed until the end.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"338\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F7600f3a31cb1630088ab7b1901ac5ae16bc1ae45.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMost of us are victims of a &#x2018;give and take&#x2019; mentality\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf I go out of my way to drive down the price of your next dream car to right near where you want it, and even beat it buy a few dollars, you probably won&#x2019;t sweat the doc fee. I may even add another ingredient to the recipe by finding better financing for you, or telling you about incentives that drive the price down. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf I give you a lot over the course of hours, you will usually give a little in a few minutes towards the end. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EReciprocity is a big influence when it comes to negotiations, And over half of Americans still like to negotiate a car deal according to a recent study by \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fpress.autotrader.com\u002F2015-03-31-New-Autotrader-Study-Consumers-Want-Big-Changes-to-the-Car-Buying-Process\"\u003EAutotrader.com \u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x2013; with women and Millenials leading that pack.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYet most people stink at bargaining for themselves. The overwhelming majority of us are not used to negotiating when it comes to goods. And most professional dealers work hard to offer a pleasant experience when it comes to your next car. We want you to willingly pay more, and obviously negotiate a lot less, but be happy when you leave the store.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EGood dealers know how to balance your desire for a given car with the opportunity to use time to gradually wear you down. As a result, most car buyers tend to drift and focus on the big battles in the beginning, while ignoring the little ones in the end.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EFees are now commonplace\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThat $19.99 oil change which used to truly be a $19.99 oil change now has a $3.50 waste disposal fee attached to it. Many people happily pay a nickel for every plastic grocery bag they use. Banks in particular have helped transition Americans into a fee-happy marketplace; On average, there are now 30 banking fees that are charged for checking accounts, with some banks now charging as many as 50 unique fees.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis fee-oriented world is compounded by the fact that nearly all dealerships now charge a fee or two regardless of the real costs involved. You want to buy a new car? Good luck doing it without a fee. The same is true for nearly all used car dealerships. Even nationwide no-haggle dealerships that pride themselves on customer service have received millions in doc fees over the years.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESo long as you&#x2019;re willing to pay that fee, dealers will continue to be more than happy to offer it. his Experimental 200-MPH Chevy Could Sell For $2 Million","summary":"One of the rarest Chevys to ever escape GM's hands, and the test bed for Corvette captain Zora Arkus-Duntov, heads to auction for the first time next month.","body":"\u003Cp\u003EAnyone who&#x2019;s a Corvette fan should know this comic book-worthy name: Zora Arkus-Duntov. If you&#x2019;re up on Chevrolet lore, you&#x2019;ll know that Arkus-Duntov indeed holds superhero status thanks to his role as the &#x201C;Father of the Corvette.&#x201D; Born in 1909, he escaped the ravages of World War II to wind up guiding General Motors&#x2019; racing flagship that remains a sports car force.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAll of which is key prelude to an amazing machine going up for auction during the famed Pebble Beach Concours d&#x2019;Elegance on the Monterey peninsula next month. Labeled simply as a 1960 Chevrolet CERV I, the ground-scraping, Formula One-looking blue and white bullet looks like it leaped out of the frames of a &#x201C;Speed Racer&#x201D; cartoon.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAnd that&#x2019;s no idle comparison when you consider that with Arkus-Duntov at the wheel this land-shark hit 206 mph at GM&#x2019;s Milford Proving Grounds in 1964.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002F1960-chevrolet-cerv-i-in-c1436559242843.html\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F2a632692fe3d8e71119cc48b9cb0f6963c73712a.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"359\" alt=\"This Experimental 200-MPH Chevy Could Sell For $2 Million\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ELong tucked away in a series of high-profile private collections, this is the first time the CERV I - which stands for Chevrolet Engineering Research Vehicle - will be offered for sale, and is expected to fetch between $1.3 and $2 million, says RM Sotheby&#x2019;s Alain Squindo.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;The rap sheet of what this car did is a mile long, and much of it was with Zora actually behind the wheel, not to mention other racing greats,&#x201D; says Squindo, noting that the collectors who took care of the car were the kind of men who would have made sure it could run and drive.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;First and foremost, though, this car contributed greatly to Zora&#x2019;s racing mentality while he was at Chevrolet,&#x201D; he says. &#x201C;It helped forge that company&#x2019;s racing pedigree.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAs the story goes, Arkus-Duntov - who joined GM in 1953 after setting up a successful parts manufacturing business in New York with his brother - was frustrated by overheating issues with a special 1957 Corvette he was driving. So he and his High Performance Vehicle team decided they needed a mule for the purpose of testing a Corvair-type drivetrain layout.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"336\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F497b18a3224f13fbc26f97933e923a9029f2a974.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EZora Arkus-Duntov with the CERV I in 1960. Photo: Getty Images\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAs drawn up on paper, the car had to be eligible for the Indianapolis 500. Its exotic skeleton consisted of a chrom-moly steel tubular space frame that tipped the scales at a mere 125 lbs., while its wind-cheating fiberglass body by Larry Shinoda (Ford Mustang) and Tony Lapine (Porsche 928) weighed just 80 lbs. Its original powerplant was a Corvette prototype-derived 289-cubic inch V8 capable of 315 hp.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut CERV I soon took on a dizzying array of guises and challenges. In fact, it first turned its massive wheels in anger on the frightening roads of Pikes Peak in Colorado Springs, where it raced up and down a mile-long segment of the 14,000-foot mountain&#x2019;s dirt roads some 60 times.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAfter middling results in that endeavor, Arkus-Duntov headed to Riverside Raceway in California. Before a Grand Prix race there, Arkus-Duntov, Dan Gurney and Stirling Moss, legends all, zipped CERV around the track before an appreciative crowd in a respectable time.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESoon, the car would go even faster. At GM&#x2019;s Proving Grounds, Arkus-Duntov took the wheel and broke 170 mph. When he failed to win NASCAR founder Bill France&#x2019;s $10,000 challenge for a car that could hit 180 mph lapping Daytona (CERV reached 162 mph), the engineer turned to turbocharging for an added boost. The result was a 500-hp beast whose front wheels lifted off the ground upon takeoff, leading to a Shinoda restyling for improved aerodynamics.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBy 1964, CERV I was in the process of being set aside to make way for its successor, CERV II. Its last official incarnation saw it packed with its (seventh) engine, a 377-cubic inch V-8 cast by Alcoa at a reported cost of nearly $300,000. That&#x2019;s the engine that rests in the car today.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"359\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F48699265803764830b676de77d3534eb3e2abba4.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAlways possessive of his automotive children, Arkus-Duntov wouldn&#x2019;t allow CERV I to be chopped up after its four-year run. Instead, he ensured that it was restored, and in 1972 both CERV I and II were gifted to Briggs Cunningham - whose Le Mans team Arkus-Duntov had helped with - for his expansive museum in Costa Mesa, Calif.&#xA0;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhen Cunningham decided to part out his gems, CERV I wound up with noted collector Miles Collier, who then sold it to the current owner.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;There&#x2019;s so much about this car that&#x2019;s fascinating, if you&#x2019;re into racing development history,&#x201D; says Squindo. &#x201C;But then, if you&#x2019;re mainly a Corvette fan, there&#x2019;s also the fact that CERV I was the test-bed for the 1963 Corvette&#x2019;s independent suspension.&#x201D;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIndeed, for fans of America&#x2019;s supercar, that&#x2019;s enough to grant CERV I haloed status.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E","content_status":"UNPUBLISHED","td_applet_infos":[],"canonical_urls":[],"uploaded_images":[],"type":"photoset","wiki_ids":["Zora_Arkus-Duntov","Chevrolet","Vicente_Cervantes","General_Motors","Larry_Shinoda"],"yct_categories":["yct:001000993","yct:001000992","yct:001000001"],"privateTags":[],"primary_photo":0,"leadImages":[{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w175\u002Fb6f43ffeaea313ef58e2720278e9edc4175d1244.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":175,"height":116,"size_type":"175","formats":{},"types":{"image\u002Fjpeg":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w175\u002Fb6f43ffeaea313ef58e2720278e9edc4175d1244.jpg"}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w200\u002Fb6f43ffeaea313ef58e2720278e9edc4175d1244.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":200,"height":133,"size_type":"200","formats":{},"types":{"image\u002Fjpeg":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w200\u002Fb6f43ffeaea313ef58e2720278e9edc4175d1244.jpg"}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w250\u002Fb6f43ffeaea313ef58e2720278e9edc4175d1244.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":250,"height":166,"size_type":"250","formats":{},"types":{"image\u002Fjpeg":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w250\u002Fb6f43ffeaea313ef58e2720278e9edc4175d1244.jpg"}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w300\u002Fb6f43ffeaea313ef58e2720278e9edc4175d1244.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":300,"height":200,"size_type":"300","formats":{},"types":{"image\u002Fjpeg":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w300\u002Fb6f43ffeaea313ef58e2720278e9edc4175d1244.jpg"}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w350\u00
